repository                <ul><li>             <a href="https://github.com/tyetech/portage"><font color="#0066cc">tyetech/portage</font></a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<h1 lang="en">Application programming interface</h1><span style="display:inline!important;float:none;background-color:rgb(255,255,255);color:rgb(34,34,34);direction:ltr;font-family:sans-serif;font-size:16px;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:normal;text-align:left;text-decoration:none;text-indent:0px;text-transform:none;white-space:normal;word-spacing:0px">			</span><div style="background-color:transparent;color:rgb(34,34,34);font-family:sans-serif;font-size:13.93px;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:normal;line-height:22.28px;text-align:left;text-decoration:none;text-indent:0px;text-transform:none;white-space:normal;word-spacing:0px">				<div style="display:block;font-size:12.8px">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div style="color:rgb(84,89,93);font-size:11.73px;line-height:14.08px;margin-bottom:16.42px;margin-left:11.73px;margin-right:0px;margin-top:0px;width:1506.13px"></div>				<div style="font-size:13.93px;line-height:22.28px"></div>				<a style="background-color:transparent;background-image:none;background-repeat:repeat;border-bottom-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-bottom-style:none;border-bottom-width:0px;border-left-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-left-style:none;border-left-width:0px;border-right-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-right-style:none;border-right-width:0px;border-top-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-top-style:none;border-top-width:0px;color:rgb(6,69,173);display:block;height:1px;overflow:hidden;padding-bottom:0px;padding-left:0px;padding-right:0px;padding-top:0px;text-decoration:none;width:1px" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>				<a style="background-color:transparent;background-image:none;background-repeat:repeat;border-bottom-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-bottom-style:none;border-bottom-width:0px;border-left-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-left-style:none;border-left-width:0px;border-right-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-right-style:none;border-right-width:0px;border-top-color:rgb(6,69,173);border-top-style:none;border-top-width:0px;color:rgb(6,69,173);display:block;height:1px;overflow:hidden;padding-bottom:0px;padding-left:0px;padding-right:0px;padding-top:0px;text-decoration:none;width:1px" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#p-search">Jump to search</a>				<div lang="en" style="direction:ltr" dir="ltr"><div style="direction:ltr"><div style="font-style:italic;margin-bottom:6.96px;padding-left:22.29px">"API" redirects here. For other uses, see <a title="API (disambiguation)" style="background-color:transparent;background-image:none;background-repeat:repeat;color:rgb(6,69,173);text-decoration:none" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/API_(disambiguation)"><font color="#0645ad">API (disambiguation)</font></a>.</div><p style="line-height:22.28px;margin-bottom:6.96px;margin-left:0px;margin-right:0px;margin-top:6.96px">In <a title="Programming language" style="background-color:transparent;background-image:none;background-repeat:repeat;color:rgb(6,69,173);text-decoration:none" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language"><font color="#0645ad">computer programming</font></a>, an <b style="line-height:22.28px;margin-bottom:0px;margin-left:0px;margin-right:0px;margin-top:0px">application programming interface</b> (<b style="line-height:22.28px;margin-bottom:0px;margin-left:0px;margin-right:0px;margin-top:0px">API</b>) is a set of subroutine definitions, <a title="Communication protocols" style="background-color:transparent;background-image:none;background-repeat:repeat;color:rgb(6,69,173);text-decoration:none" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_protocols"><font color="#0645ad">communication protocol</font></a></p></div></div></div> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <a title="Communication protocols" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_protocols"><font color="#0066cc">communication protocols</font></a>, and tools for building software. In general terms, it is a set of clearly defined methods of communication among various components. A good API makes it easier to develop a <a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program"><font color="#0066cc">computer program</font></a> by providing all the building blocks, which are then put together by the <a title="Programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmer"><font color="#0066cc">programmer</font></a>. </li></ul></div></h1></div></div><div><div><div><div style="display:block"><div><div><div><div><div><div lang="en" dir="ltr"><div><h1><p>An API may  be for a web-based system, <a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system"><font color="#0066cc">operating system</font></a>, <a title="Database system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_system"><font color="#0066cc">database system</font></a>, computer hardware, or <a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)"><font color="#0066cc">software library</font></a>. </p><p>An API specification can take many forms, but often includes specifications for <a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine"><font color="#0066cc">routines</font></a>, <a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure"><font color="#0066cc">data structures</font></a>, <a title="Class (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)"><font color="#0066cc">object classes</font></a>, <a title="Variable (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(computer_science)"><font color="#0066cc">variables</font></a>, or <a title="Remote procedure call" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remote_procedure_call"><font color="#0066cc">remote calls</font></a>. <a title="POSIX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX"><font color="#0066cc">POSIX</font></a>, <a title="Windows API" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_API"><font color="#0066cc">Windows API</font></a> and <a title="Advanced SCSI programming interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_SCSI_programming_interface"><font color="#0066cc">ASPI</font></a> are examples of different forms of APIs. Documentation for the API usually is provided to facilitate usage and implementation. </p></h1><div><div lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2></div><h1><ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Purpose"><font color="#0066cc">1Purpose</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Uses"><font color="#0066cc">2Uses</font></a><ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Libraries_and_frameworks"><font color="#0066cc">2.1Libraries and frameworks</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Operating_systems"><font color="#0066cc">2.2Operating systems</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Remote_APIs"><font color="#0066cc">2.3Remote APIs</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Web_APIs"><font color="#0066cc">2.4Web APIs</font></a></li></ul></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Design"><font color="#0066cc">3Design</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Release_policies"><font color="#0066cc">4Release policies</font></a><ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Public_API_implications"><font color="#0066cc">4.1Public API implications</font></a></li></ul></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Documentation"><font color="#0066cc">5Documentation</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Copyright_controversy"><font color="#0066cc">6Copyright controversy</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Examples"><font color="#0066cc">7Examples</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#See_also"><font color="#0066cc">8See also</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#References"><font color="#0066cc">9References</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Further_reading"><font color="#0066cc">10Further reading</font></a></li></ul></h1></div><h2>Purpose[<a title="Edit section: Purpose" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><p>Just as a <a title="Graphical user interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphical_user_interface"><font color="#0066cc">graphical user interface</font></a> (GUI) makes it easier for people to use programs, application programming interfaces make it easier for developers to use certain technologies in building applications. An API simplifies programming by <a title="Abstraction (software engineering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstraction_(software_engineering)"><font color="#0066cc">abstracting</font></a> the underlying implementation and only exposing objects or actions the developer needs. While a graphical interface for an <a title="Email client" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email_client"><font color="#0066cc">email client</font></a> might provide a user with a button that performs all the steps for fetching and highlighting new emails, an API for file <a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output"><font color="#0066cc">input/output</font></a> might give the developer a <a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine"><font color="#0066cc">function</font></a> that copies a file from one location to another without requiring that the developer understand the <a title="Journaling file system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journaling_file_system"><font color="#0066cc">file system</font></a> operations occurring behind the scenes.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Clarke4-1"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[1]</font></a></sup> </p><p>The modern API management helps the enterprises expose individual components in well-documented services that the internal developers and partners can use to rapidly iterate new features.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-2"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[2]</font></a></sup> </p></h1><h2>Uses[<a title="Edit section: Uses" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h3>Libraries and frameworks[<a title="Edit section: Libraries and frameworks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h3><h1><p>An API usually is related to a <a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)"><font color="#0066cc">software library</font></a>. The API describes and prescribes the "expected behavior" (a specification) while the library is an "actual implementation" of this set of rules. </p><p>A single API can have multiple implementations (or none, being abstract) in the form of different libraries that share the same programming interface. </p><p>The separation of the API from its implementation can allow programs written in one language to use a library written in another. For example, because <a title="Scala (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scala_(programming_language)"><font color="#0066cc">Scala</font></a> and <a title="Java (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_(programming_language)"><font color="#0066cc">Java</font></a> compile to compatible <a title="Bytecode" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bytecode"><font color="#0066cc">bytecode</font></a>, Scala developers can take advantage of any Java API.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-OderskySpoonVenners8-3"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[3]</font></a></sup> </p><p>API use can vary depending on the type of programming language involved. An API for a <a title="Procedural programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedural_programming"><font color="#0066cc">procedural language</font></a> such as <a title="Lua (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lua_(programming_language)"><font color="#0066cc">Lua</font></a> could consist primarily of basic routines to execute code, manipulate data or handle errors while an API for an <a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming"><font color="#0066cc">object-oriented language</font></a>, such as Java, would provide a specification of classes and its <a title="Class method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_method"><font color="#0066cc">class methods</font></a>.<font size="2"><font color="#0066cc"><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Sintes16-5">[5]</a></sup></font></font> </p><p><a title="Language binding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_binding"><font color="#0066cc">Language bindings</font></a> are also APIs. By mapping the features and capabilities of one language to an interface implemented in another language, a language binding allows a library or service written in one language to be used when developing in another language.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Emery-6"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[6]</font></a></sup> Tools such as <a title="SWIG" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SWIG"><font color="#0066cc">SWIG</font></a> and F2PY, a <a title="Fortran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortran"><font color="#0066cc">Fortran</font></a>-to-<a title="Python (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Python_(programming_language)"><font color="#0066cc">Python</font></a> interface generator, facilitate the creation of such interfaces.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-7"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[7]</font></a></sup> </p><p>An API can also be related to a <a title="Framework (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Framework_(computer_science)"><font color="#0066cc">software framework</font></a>: a framework can be based on several libraries implementing several APIs, but unlike the normal use of an API, the access to the behavior built into the framework is mediated by extending its content with new classes plugged into the framework itself. </p><p>Moreover, the overall program flow of control can be out of the control of the caller and in the hands of the framework by <a title="Inversion of control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inversion_of_control"><font color="#0066cc">inversion of control</font></a> or a similar mechanism.<font size="2"><font color="#0066cc"><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></font></font> </p></h1><h3>Operating systems[<a title="Edit section: Operating systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h3><h1><p>An API can specify the interface between an application and the <a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system"><font color="#0066cc">operating system</font></a>.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Oreilly91-10"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[10]</font></a></sup> <a title="POSIX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX"><font color="#0066cc">POSIX</font></a>, for example, specifies a set of common APIs that aim to enable an application written for a POSIX conformant operating system to be <a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler"><font color="#0066cc">compiled</font></a> for another POSIX conformant operating system. </p><p><a title="Linux" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linux"><font color="#0066cc">Linux</font></a> and <a title="Berkeley Software Distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berkeley_Software_Distribution"><font color="#0066cc">Berkeley Software Distribution</font></a> are examples of operating systems that implement the POSIX APIs.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-WestDedrick16-11"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[11]</font></a></sup> </p><p><a title="Microsoft" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft"><font color="#0066cc">Microsoft</font></a> has shown a strong commitment to a backward-compatible API, particularly within its <a title="Windows API" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_API"><font color="#0066cc">Windows API</font></a> (Win32) library, so older applications may run on newer versions of Windows using an executable-specific setting called "Compatibility Mode".<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-12"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[12]</font></a></sup> </p><p>An API differs from an <a title="Application binary interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_binary_interface"><font color="#0066cc">application binary interface</font></a> (ABI) in that an API is source code based while an ABI is <a title="Binary file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_file"><font color="#0066cc">binary</font></a> based. For instance, <a title="POSIX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX"><font color="#0066cc">POSIX</font></a> provides APIs while the <a title="Linux Standard Base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linux_Standard_Base"><font color="#0066cc">Linux Standard Base</font></a> provides an ABI.<font size="2"><font color="#0066cc"><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></font></font> </p></h1><h3>Remote APIs[<a title="Edit section: Remote APIs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h3><h1><p>Remote APIs allow developers to manipulate remote resources through <a title="Communications protocol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communications_protocol"><font color="#0066cc">protocols</font></a>, specific standards for communication that allow different technologies to work together, regardless of language or platform. For example, the Java Database Connectivity API allows developers to query many different types of <a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database"><font color="#0066cc">databases</font></a> with the same set of functions, while the <a title="Java remote method invocation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_remote_method_invocation"><font color="#0066cc">Java remote method invocation</font></a> API uses the <a title="Java Remote Method Protocol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_Remote_Method_Protocol"><font color="#0066cc">Java Remote Method Protocol</font></a> to allow <a title="Remote procedure call" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remote_procedure_call"><font color="#0066cc">invocation</font></a> of functions that operate remotely, but appear local to the developer.<font size="2"><font color="#0066cc"><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Bierhoff9-15">[15]</a></sup><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Wilson16-16">[16]</a></sup></font></font> </p><p>Therefore, remote APIs are useful in maintaining the object abstraction in <a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming"><font color="#0066cc">object-oriented programming</font></a>; a method call, executed locally on a proxy object, invokes the corresponding method on the remote object, using the remoting protocol, and acquires the result to be used locally as return value. </p><p>A modification on the proxy object also will result in a corresponding modification on the remote object.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-AdvancedCorba-17"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[17]</font></a></sup> </p></h1><h3>Web APIs[<a title="Edit section: Web APIs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h3><h1><div>Main article: <a title="Web API" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_API"><font color="#0066cc">Web API</font></a></div><p>Web APIs are the defined interfaces through which interactions happen between an enterprise and applications that use its assets, which also is a Service Level Agreement (SLA) to specify the functional provider and expose the service path or URL for its API users. An API approach is an architectural approach that revolves around providing a program interface to a set of services to different applications serving different types of consumers.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-18"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[18]</font></a></sup> </p><p>When used in the context of <a title="Web development tools" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_development_tools"><font color="#0066cc">web development</font></a>, an API is typically defined as a set of specifications, such as <a title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol"><font color="#0066cc">Hypertext Transfer Protocol</font></a> (HTTP) request messages, along with a definition of the structure of response messages, usually in an Extensible Markup Language (<a title="XML" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XML"><font color="#0066cc">XML</font></a>) or JavaScript Object Notation (<a title="JSON" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JSON"><font color="#0066cc">JSON</font></a>) format. An example might be a shipping company API that can be added to an eCommerce-focused website to facilitate ordering shipping services and automatically include current shipping rates, without the site developer having to enter the shipper's rate table into a web database. While "web API" historically virtually has been synonymous for <a title="Web service" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_service"><font color="#0066cc">web service</font></a>, the recent trend (so-called <a title="Web 2.0" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_2.0"><font color="#0066cc">Web 2.0</font></a>) has been moving away from Simple Object Access Protocol (<a title="SOAP" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SOAP"><font color="#0066cc">SOAP</font></a>) based web services and <a title="Service-oriented architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Service-oriented_architecture"><font color="#0066cc">service-oriented architecture</font></a> (SOA) towards more direct <a title="Representational state transfer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Representational_state_transfer"><font color="#0066cc">representational state transfer</font></a> (REST) style <a title="Web resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_resource"><font color="#0066cc">web resources</font></a> and <a title="Resource-oriented architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource-oriented_architecture"><font color="#0066cc">resource-oriented architecture</font></a> (ROA).<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-19"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[19]</font></a></sup> Part of this trend is related to the <a title="Semantic Web" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_Web"><font color="#0066cc">Semantic Web</font></a> movement toward <a title="Resource Description Framework" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework"><font color="#0066cc">Resource Description Framework</font></a> (RDF), a concept to promote web-based <a title="Ontology engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_engineering"><font color="#0066cc">ontology engineering</font></a> technologies. Web APIs allow the combination of multiple APIs into new applications known as <a title="Mashup (web application hybrid)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashup_(web_application_hybrid)"><font color="#0066cc">mashups</font></a>.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-20"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[20]</font></a></sup> In the social media space, web APIs have allowed web communities to facilitate sharing content and data between communities and applications. In this way, content that is created in one place dynamically can be posted and updated to multiple locations on the web.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Parr16-21"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[21]</font></a></sup> For example, Twitter's REST API allows developers to access core Twitter data and the Search API provides methods for developers to interact with Twitter Search and trends data.<sup style="white-space:nowrap"><font size="2">[<i><a title="Wikipedia:Citation needed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)"><font color="#0066cc">citation needed</font></span></a></i>]</font></sup> </p></h1><h2>Design[<a title="Edit section: Design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><p>The design of an API has significant impact on its usage.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Clarke4-1"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[1]</font></a></sup> The principle of <a title="Information hiding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_hiding"><font color="#0066cc">information hiding</font></a> describes the role of programming interfaces as enabling <a title="Modular programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modular_programming"><font color="#0066cc">modular programming</font></a> by hiding the implementation details of the modules so that users of modules need not understand the complexities inside the modules.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Parnas72-22"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[22]</font></a></sup> Thus, the design of an API attempts to provide only the tools a user would expect.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Clarke4-1"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[1]</font></a></sup> The design of programming interfaces represents an important part of <a title="Software architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_architecture"><font color="#0066cc">software architecture</font></a>, the organization of a complex piece of software.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-GarlanShaw94-23"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[23]</font></a></sup> </p><p>Several authors have created recommendations for how to design APIs, such as <a title="Joshua Bloch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joshua_Bloch"><font color="#0066cc">Joshua Bloch</font></a>,<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-24"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[24]</font></a></sup> Kin Lane,<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-25"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[25]</font></a></sup> and Michi Henning.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-26"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[26]</font></a></sup> </p></h1><h2>Release policies[<a title="Edit section: Release policies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><p>APIs are one of the more common ways technology companies integrate with each other. Those that provide and use APIs are considered as being members of a business ecosystem.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-27"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[27]</font></a></sup> </p><p>The main policies for releasing an API are:<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Boyd16-28"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[28]</font></a></sup> </p><ul><li><u>Private</u>: The API is for internal company use only.</li><li><u>Partner</u>: Only specific business partners can use the API. For example, <a title="Transportation network company" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_network_company"><font color="#0066cc">car service companies</font></a> such as <a title="Uber (company)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uber_(company)"><font color="#0066cc">Uber</font></a> and <a title="Lyft" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyft"><font color="#0066cc">Lyft</font></a> allow approved third-party developers to directly order rides from within their apps. This allows the companies to exercise quality control by curating which apps have access to the API, and provides them with an additional revenue stream.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-Weissbrot16-29"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[29]</font></a></sup></li><li><u>Public</u>: The API is available for use by the public. For example, <a title="Microsoft" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft"><font color="#0066cc">Microsoft</font></a> makes the <a title="Microsoft Windows" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows"><font color="#0066cc">Microsoft Windows</font></a> API public, and <a title="Apple Inc." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc."><font color="#0066cc">Apple</font></a> releases its APIs <a title="Carbon (API)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_(API)"><font color="#0066cc">Carbon</font></a> and <a title="Cocoa (API)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cocoa_(API)"><font color="#0066cc">Cocoa</font></a>, so that software can be written for their <a title="Computing platform" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing_platform"><font color="#0066cc">platforms</font></a>.</li></ul></h1><h3>Public API implications[<a title="Edit section: Public API implications" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h3><h1><p>An important factor when an API becomes public is its "interface stability". Changes by a developer to a part of it—for example adding new parameters to a function call—could break compatibility with clients that depend on that API.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-30"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[30]</font></a></sup> </p><p>When parts of a publicly presented API are subject to change and thus not stable, such parts of a particular API should be documented explicitly as "unstable". For example, in the <a title="Google Guava" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Guava"><font color="#0066cc">Google Guava</font></a> library, the parts that are considered unstable, and that might change in the near future, are marked with the <a title="Java annotation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_annotation"><font color="#0066cc">Java annotation</font></a> <code>@Beta</code>.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-31"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[31]</font></a></sup> </p><p>A public API can sometimes declare parts of itself as <i><a title="Deprecation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deprecation"><font color="#0066cc">deprecated</font></a></i> or rescinded. This usually means that part of the API should be considered a candidate for being removed, or modified in a backward incompatible way. Therefore, these changes allows developers to transition away from parts of the API that will be removed or not supported in the future.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-OracleDeprecation16-32"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[32]</font></a></sup> </p><p>For any library with a significant user base, as soon as an element becomes part of the public API, it starts being used in diverse ways.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-MendezBaudry2013-33"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[33]</font></a></sup> In this perspective, client code sometimes contain original or opportunistic usages that were never envisioned by the API designers. </p></h1><h2>Documentation[<a title="Edit section: Documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><p>API documentation describes what services an API offers and how to use those services, aiming to cover everything a client would need to know for practical purposes. </p><p>Documentation is crucial for the development and maintenance of applications using the API.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-DekelHerbsleb9-34"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[34]</font></a></sup> API documentation is traditionally found in documentation files but can also be found in social media such as blogs, forums, and Q&amp;A websites.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-ParninTreude11-35"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[35]</font></a></sup> </p><p>Traditional documentation files are often presented via a documentation system, such as <a title="Javadoc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Javadoc"><font color="#0066cc">Javadoc</font></a> or <a title="Pydoc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pydoc"><font color="#0066cc">Pydoc</font></a>, that has a consistent appearance and structure. However, the types of content included in the documentation differs from API to API.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-MaalejRobillard12-36"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[36]</font></a></sup> </p><p>In the interest of clarity, API documentation may include a description of classes and methods in the API as well as "typical usage scenarios, code snippets, design rationales, performance discussions, and contracts", but implementation details of the API services themselves are usually omitted. </p><p>Restrictions and limitations on how the API can be used are also covered by the documentation. For instance, documentation for an API function could note that its parameters cannot be null, that the function itself is not <a title="Thread safety" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thread_safety"><font color="#0066cc">thread safe</font></a>,<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-MonperrusEichberg11-37"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[37]</font></a></sup> or that a <a title="Increment and decrement operators" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Increment_and_decrement_operators"><font color="#0066cc">decrement</font></a> and cancel protocol averts self-trading.<sup style="margin-left:0.1em;white-space:nowrap"><font size="2">[<i><a title="Wikipedia:Please clarify" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify"><span title="explanation required (February 2018)"><font color="#0066cc">clarification needed</font></span></a></i>]</font></sup> Because API documentation tends to be comprehensive, it is a challenge for writers to keep the documentation updated and for users to read it carefully, potentially yielding <a title="Software bug" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_bug"><font color="#0066cc">bugs</font></a>.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-38"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[38]</font></a></sup> </p><p>API documentation can be enriched with <a title="Metadata" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metadata"><font color="#0066cc">metadata</font></a> information like <a title="Java annotation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_annotation"><font color="#0066cc">Java annotations</font></a>. This metadata can be used by the compiler, tools, and by the <i>run-time</i> environment to implement custom behaviors or custom handling.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-39"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[39]</font></a></sup> </p><p>It is possible to generate API documentation in data-driven manner. By observing a large number of programs that use a given API, it is possible to infer the typical usages, as well the required contracts and directives.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-40"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[40]</font></a></sup> Then, templates can be used to generate natural language from the mined data. </p></h1><h2>Copyright controversy[<a title="Edit section: Copyright controversy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><div>Main article: <a title="Oracle America, Inc. v. Google, Inc." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oracle_America,_Inc._v._Google,_Inc."><font color="#0066cc">Oracle America, Inc. v. Google, Inc.</font></a></div><p>In 2010, <a title="Oracle Corporation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oracle_Corporation"><font color="#0066cc">Oracle Corporation</font></a> sued <a title="Google" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google"><font color="#0066cc">Google</font></a> for having distributed a new implementation of Java embedded in the <a title="Android (operating system)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Android_(operating_system)"><font color="#0066cc">Android</font></a> operating system.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-41"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[41]</font></a></sup> Google had not acquired any permission to reproduce the Java API, although permission had been given to the similar <a title="OpenJDK" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenJDK"><font color="#0066cc">OpenJDK</font></a> project. Judge <a title="William Alsup" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Alsup"><font color="#0066cc">William Alsup</font></a> ruled in the <i><a title="Oracle v. Google" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oracle_v._Google"><font color="#0066cc">Oracle v. Google</font></a></i> case that APIs cannot be <a title="Copyrighted" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyrighted"><font color="#0066cc">copyrighted</font></a> in the U.S, and that a victory for Oracle would have widely expanded copyright protection and allowed the copyrighting of simple software commands: </p><blockquote><p>To accept Oracle's claim would be to allow anyone to copyright one version of code to carry out a system of commands and thereby bar all others from writing its own different versions to carry out all or part of the same commands.<font size="2"><font color="#0066cc"><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></font></font></p></blockquote><p>In 2014, however, Alsup's ruling was overturned on appeal, though the question of whether such use of APIs constitutes <a title="Fair use" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_use"><font color="#0066cc">fair use</font></a> was left unresolved.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-44"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[44]</font></a></sup> </p><p>In 2016, following a two-week trial, a jury determined that Google's reimplementation of the Java API constituted fair use, but Oracle vowed to appeal the decision.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-45"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[45]</font></a></sup> Oracle won on its appeal, with the <a title="United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Federal_Circuit"><font color="#0066cc">Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit</font></a> ruling that Google's use of the APIs did not qualify for fair use.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#cite_note-bbn_march2018-46"><font color="#0066cc" size="2">[46]</font></a></sup> </p></h1><h2>Examples[<a title="Edit section: Examples" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><div>Main category: <a title="Category:Application programming interfaces" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Application_programming_interfaces"><font color="#0066cc">Application programming interfaces</font></a></div><div><ul><li><a title="Advanced SCSI programming interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_SCSI_programming_interface"><font color="#0066cc">ASPI</font></a> for <a title="SCSI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SCSI"><font color="#0066cc">SCSI</font></a> device interfacing</li><li><a title="Cocoa (API)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cocoa_(API)"><font color="#0066cc">Cocoa</font></a> and <a title="Carbon (API)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_(API)"><font color="#0066cc">Carbon</font></a> for the <a title="Macintosh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh"><font color="#0066cc">Macintosh</font></a></li><li><a title="DirectX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DirectX"><font color="#0066cc">DirectX</font></a> for <a title="Microsoft Windows" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows"><font color="#0066cc">Microsoft Windows</font></a></li><li><a title="EHLLAPI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EHLLAPI"><font color="#0066cc">EHLLAPI</font></a></li><li><a title="List of Java APIs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Java_APIs"><font color="#0066cc">Java APIs</font></a></li><li><a title="Open Database Connectivity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_Database_Connectivity"><font color="#0066cc">ODBC</font></a> for <a title="Microsoft Windows" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows"><font color="#0066cc">Microsoft Windows</font></a></li><li><a title="OpenAL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenAL"><font color="#0066cc">OpenAL</font></a> cross-platform sound API</li><li><a title="OpenCL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCL"><font color="#0066cc">OpenCL</font></a> cross-platform API for general-purpose computing for CPUs &amp; GPUs</li><li><a title="OpenGL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenGL"><font color="#0066cc">OpenGL</font></a> cross-platform graphics API</li><li><a title="OpenMP" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenMP"><font color="#0066cc">OpenMP</font></a> API that supports multi-platform shared memory multiprocessing programming in C, C++ and Fortran on many architectures, including Unix and Microsoft Windows platforms.</li><li><a title="Server Application Programming Interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_Application_Programming_Interface"><font color="#0066cc">Server Application Programming Interface</font></a> (SAPI)</li><li><a title="Simple DirectMedia Layer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simple_DirectMedia_Layer"><font color="#0066cc">Simple DirectMedia Layer</font></a> (SDL)</li></ul></div></h1><h2>See also[<a title="Edit section: See also" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Application_programming_interface&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"><font color="#0066cc">edit</font></a>]</h2><h1><div><ul><li><a title="API testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/API_testing"><font color="#0066cc">API testing</font></a></li><li><a title="API writer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/API_writer"><font color="#0066cc">API writer</font></a></li><li><a title="Calling convention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calling_convention"><font color="#0066cc">Calling convention</font></a></li><li><a title="Comparison of application virtual machines" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparison_of_application_virtual_machines"><font color="#0066cc">Comparison of application virtual machines</font></a></li><li><a title="Common Object Request Broker Architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_Object_Request_Broker_Architecture"><font color="#0066cc">Common Object Request Broker Architecture</font></a> (CORBA)</li><li><a title="Document Object Model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Document_Object_Model"><font color="#0066cc">Document Object Model</font></a> (DOM)</li><li><a title="Double-chance function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double-chance_function"><font color="#0066cc">Double-chance function</font></a></li><li><a title="Foreign function interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_function_interface"><font color="#0066cc">Foreign function interface</font></a></li><li><a title="Interface (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interface_(computing)"><font color="#0066cc">Interface (computing)</font></a></li><li><a title="Interface control document" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interface_control_document"><font color="#0066cc">Interface control document</font></a></li><li><a title="List of 3D graphics APIs" For other uses, see <a title="API (disambiguation)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/API_(disambiguation)"><font color="#0066cc">API (disambiguation)</font></a>.</div><p>In <a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language"><font color="#0066cc">computer programming</font></a>, an application programming interface (API) is a set of subroutine definitions, <a title="Communication protocols" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_protocols"><font color="#0066cc">communication protocols</font></a>, and tools for building software. In general terms, it is a set of clearly defined methods of communication among various components. A good API makes it easier to develop a <a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program"><font color="#0066cc">computer program</font></a> by providing all the building blocks, which are then put together by the <a title="Programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmer"><font color="#0066cc">programmer</font></a>. </p><p>An API may  be for a web-based system, <a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system"><font color="#0066cc">operating system</font></a>, <a title="Database system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_system"><font color="#0066cc">database system</font></a>, computer hardware, or <a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)"><font color="#0066cc">software library</font></a>. </p><p>An API specification can take many forms, but often includes specifications for <a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine"><font color="#0066cc">routines</font></a>, <a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure"><font color="#0066cc">data structures</font></a>, <a title="Class (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)"><font color="#0066cc">object classes</font></a>, <a title="Variable (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(computer_science)"><font color="#0066cc">variables</font></a>, or <a title="Remote procedure call" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remote_procedure_call"><font color="#0066cc">remote calls</font></a>. <a title="POSIX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX"><font color="#0066cc">POSIX</font></a>, <a title="Windows API" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_API"><font color="#0066cc">Windows API</font></a> and <a title="Advanced SCSI programming interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_SCSI_programming_interface"><font color="#0066cc">ASPI</font></a> are examples of different forms of APIs. Documentation for the API usually is provided to facilitate usage and implementation. </p></h1><div><div lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2></div><h1><ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Purpose"><font color="#0066cc">1Purpose</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Uses"><font color="#0066cc">2Uses</font></a><ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Operating_systems"><font color="#0066cc">2.2Operating systems</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Remote_APIs"><font color="#0066cc">2.3Remote APIs</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Web_APIs"><font color="#0066cc">2.4Web APIs</font></a></li></ul></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Design"><font color="#0066cc">3Design</font></a></li><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface#Release_policies"><font color="#0066cc">4Release policies</font></a><ul><li><a
